    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_more_filters_span_tip_902').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer17461318268869129543">So.... I actually did not mind this book... Similar to the first. I did not mind the first either. I actually like the story that the author is trying to pull off... I just don't think she is very good at it. She plays her characters off as stupid. Especially in this one. The whole pregnancy theme is the EXACT same as the first where they don't realize they are pregnant... Although ALL the signs are there and they have had unprotected sex multiple times during there heat cycle.... It just doesn'</span>
  <span id="freeText17461318268869129543" style="display:none">So.... I actually did not mind this book... Similar to the first. I did not mind the first either. I actually like the story that the author is trying to pull off... I just don't think she is very good at it. She plays her characters off as stupid. Especially in this one. The whole pregnancy theme is the EXACT same as the first where they don't realize they are pregnant... Although ALL the signs are there and they have had unprotected sex multiple times during there heat cycle.... It just doesn't make sense that they wouldn't even consider the possibility... Very annoying when she makes them play dumb when they announce their symptoms. I also just don't feel alex... First she is a tough girl then she lets comrade boss her around and giggles and smiles at him after and then she is a tough girl again? She is so inconsistent. The author also says the same statements over and over again... Especially when she switches characters that's are narrating. They will literally say the same thing just in a different sequence. She doesn't even change up the words... I honestly do like the "idea" of this series but the writing could have been better. There are also tons of grammatical errors... Which I feel is weird for a published book... Anywho, that's why only two stars. </span>

I felt like Alex just had way to much tragedy in her life & then never being able to have a pup just put the cherry on her cake of misery. Comrade had definitely changed but talk about a crappy way to treat a mate. I just had a hard time getting past that as well. The ending </span>
  <span id="freeText10513225918683217104" style="display:none">I loved the 1st book in the series w/ the story of Axel &amp; Celena and I truely did want to love comrade and alex's story but I couldn't. No matter how much I wanted to really get emersed in this book it just wasn't the same. I felt like Alex just had way to much tragedy in her life &amp; then never being able to have a pup just put the cherry on her cake of misery. Comrade had definitely changed but talk about a crappy way to treat a mate. I just had a hard time getting past that as well. The ending was completely rushed. Fastforwarding to when the triplets were teenagers just hurried everything along way to much and left so many unanswered questions. Part of me hopes there will be a 3rd book so there can be some closure on some of the characters and what happened during their lives but another part isn't sure if that's what I really want. If everything is rushed along the same way with gaping holes I don't think I'd enjoy a 3rd book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10513225918683217104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979304389" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15823650885456547826">I hate, hate, hate the main character Alex. She is a selfish bitch. It's all me, me. me with her. My dad won't talk to me, my alpha told me to do my job and I got pissy with him about it. My mate told a teenager he loved her and I freaked the f**k out about it without finding out why he said it. My mate nearly died and while he was in a coma I found out I was pregnant but did nothing to look after the baby because I was too busy feeling sorry for myself. When my mate finally wake up I just cry a</span>
  <span id="freeText15823650885456547826" style="display:none">I hate, hate, hate the main character Alex. She is a selfish bitch. It's all me, me. me with her. My dad won't talk to me, my alpha told me to do my job and I got pissy with him about it. My mate told a teenager he loved her and I freaked the f**k out about it without finding out why he said it. My mate nearly died and while he was in a coma I found out I was pregnant but did nothing to look after the baby because I was too busy feeling sorry for myself. When my mate finally wake up I just cry and fall asleep without explaining anything to him. <br />I don't like how the book skips years and months ahead of time without letting the reading know it's gonna happen. And the ending is so abrupt.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0n0wvJ9Unn4CjsWp+SX5jAQPK1pa7/4TPmG+bwFJGOVWsxzMMh9jFnsBnVeuYp+BDXeg6mvwvn3x7/oFl1rBiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('E2goIe/8rsO2Uc2IhwuGNPMRpk1EdqbMbs/4BV+g3YmXpgRRQrdTq8/elXbQTOA5+mkt/XVp5qKhQbxvybME5w==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText15448755699644742962" style="display:none">Violet Samuels lives in Australia, being half Australian and half Portuguese, and is a young girl/woman that is still in her youth. Even for being young, she's never lived in one place for more than two years. However, the favourite place she has lived was on the Whitsunday's. Violet loved the Whitsunday's because it's where Unique Different Found all began and it's where her friends convinced her to go for it and have a go. Look at where that's brought her. Violet's passion she is most dedicated to is her dancing, acting and singing. She has been doing classical ballet since she was four, including other dance styles on the way. She's always been able to sing and always been able to act. She's been able to use these skills in different plays, musicals, dance concerts and eisteddfods. Violet Samuels is a bubbly and energetic girl/woman who is kind, caring and has a big heart. She loves to dance, sing and act and can't wait for so many people to read her book to let them escape from the rest of the world, even just for a little while.</span>
